 P. 83. **महाहि** &c.—S'aṅk. should have drawn her attention to the immensely great size of Garuḍa. **मस्तिष्क**— the brain. **रक्तच्छटा**—streams of blood. See com. **चण्डचञ्चुः**— He refers to Garuda's beak, because that at once distinguishes him from other men क्व क्व when repeated in co-ordinate sentences implies great disparity or incogruity; cf. क्व सूर्यप्रभवो वंशः क्व चाल्पविषया मतिः । Rag. I. 2. क्व बत हरिणकानां जीवितं चातिलोलं क्व च निशितनिपाता वज्रसाराः शरास्ते। S'ak. I. 10. **असौ**— generally refers to a person or thing at a distance; cf अदसस्तु विप्रकृष्टं तदिति परोक्षे विजानीयात्। सः would have been better.

 ** सत्त्वस्वभावा**—is best taken as सत्त्वानुरूपा in keeping with his internal goodness; i. e. whose disposition and external form bear testimony to his सत्त्व. The Triv. Ed. reads सोमसौम्यस्वभावाकृतिः where सोमसौम्य means pleasing and gentle like the Moon; but hero सोम has no propriety. सौम्यस्वभावरूपाकृतिः—means 'Having a mellow disposition, general appearance and form.'

 **साधुः**—A kind-hearted or good man (ready to relieve the distress of others); cf. तं विस्मितं धेनुरुवाच साधो। Rag. II. 62, and below s'l. 15.

 **मा भैषीः**—The augment अ of the Aor. is dropped after the prohibitive particle मा. धीरा—One who has taken up courage; calm; composed. **चिरं जीव**—She gives this blessing as necessary at the time; for he was to save her son from the jaws of Garudda, which meant peril to his life. She does not know as yet how he was to save her son.

 ** प्रावृत्य**— Having covered; the object to this is स्वदेहं **यावत्—**has the sense of 'determination' here; I will assuredly give &e; or, it may go with ददामि and give it the sense of immediate futurity.

 P.84 **प्रतिहतम**— May the evil be averted. This like शान्तं पापं (see page 96) is used in dramas when one hears some- thing unpleasant and which one likes to see averted. Mark how the noble-minded mother dislikes to hear the very proposal; much less she would like to see its execution, °निर्विशेषः— निर्गतः विशेषः यस्मात् not differing in anyway from, just like. Cf. संवर्धितानां सुतनिर्विशेषं Rag. V. 6; अपत्यनिर्विशेषाणि सत्त्वानि। Śák. VII. **सविषादम्**—He was sorry to see that Jimúta. was ready to sacrifice his life for himself जगद्विपरीतं— Against the ways of the world; extraordinary, quite unique.

** विश्वामित्रःः**—see com.; विश्वस्य मित्रं विश्वं मित्रमस्येति वा; tho अ of विश्व is lengthened before मित्र when the whole refers to the Ṛishi of that name; otherwise विश्वमित्रो माणवकः श्वमांसं—i. c., the condemned of the condemned. See Manu quoted in the com.

 **Allusion**—Once a terrible famine visited the land, and food became so scarce that men thought of eating men. The sage Visvamitra feeling the pinch of hunger wandered about in quest of food. In the course of his wanderings, he came across a small village inhabited by the Chân lâlas. There at a certain house his eyes caught sight of a piece of dog's flesh. After deep consideration he came to the conclusion that there was no sin in stealing flesh for the preservation of one's life, and with that intention lay down there, watching it. At dead of night when all the Châṇḍâlas were asleep, the sage got up, and tried to take away the flesh, when a Châṇḍâla who was awake caught him in the act. On coming to know, however, that the stealer was no less a person than the great sage Vis'vâmitra, he remonstrated with him on the impropriety of such an act; but Vis'vâmitra was too much oppressed by hunger to listen to him and persuaded him to allow him to take away the flesh. But before he ate it, he thought of offering a portion of it to the gods after due worship. As he kindled the fire for that purpose and called down the gods, Indra sent down fertilizing showers. See com., and Mb. S'ântiparvan, ch. 141.

 ** नाडीजङ्घः**— Name of a king of cranes also called Rájadharman, who was renowned for his benevolence and lived on a banyan tree in a forest near the modern Allahabad. **निजघ्ने**—Pass. perf. of हन्.

 **Allusion**— Once there lived in a village in mid-India a poor and illiterate Brâlimaṇa, named Gautama. Unable to earn his livelihood in his village be wandered about for a time and coming to a forest joined a band of S'abaras and got from their chief much wealth, a house and a S'abara female slave. He lived there giving up the duties of a Brâlimaṇa, by killing birds and beasts. Once wishing to trade by sea he joined a body of merchants all of whom were killed by a wild elephant while they were passing through a dense forest. Gautama, thus left alone, wandered about for many days eating raw meat got by hunting. At last he came to a beautiful wood and rested under a banyan tree, which was the residence of Nâḍîjaṅgha. Nâḍîjaṅgha received him with hospitality due to a guest, and learning from him that he was travelling for the sake of wealth, sent him to his friend, Virúpâksha, a Râkshasa prince ruling near Ayodhyâ. Gautama, having obtained immense riches from Virûpâksha, returned, and on his way halted under the same banyan tree. Nâdîjangha again received him hospitably, fanned him with his own wings and gave him food to cat. The ungrateful Gautama, however, seeing that he had no provisions for his journey, killed and roasted the crane and went away with him. He was, however, soon caught by Virúpâksha, highly incensed at this act of ingratitude, and put to death on the same spot where the crane was killed. When Indra heard of the fate of Nâdîjangha he came down with nectar and revived him.Nâdîjangha then requested Indra to restore to life Gautama also, and the latter granted his wish.Nâdîjangha then treated Gautama affectionately and sent him away with presents. For a fuller account see Mb. Sântiparvan, chapters 168-176.

 **कश्यपः—** So called from his having drunk कश्य or wine; of. **कश्यपस्तस्य पुत्रोऽभूत्कश्यपानात्स कश्यपः।** Mârk.—P. He was the son of Marîchi, son of Brahman, one of the Prajâpatis. By his wives Aditi and Diti he was the father of the gods and the demons; and Vinatâ and Kadrû the father of Garuḍa and the serpents. See A. Dic. also.

 **उरगान्** — उरसा गच्छतीति उरगः fr. उरस् + गम् + डः (अ); the स् of उरस् is dropped irregularly; sec Vârtika on Pâṇ. III. 2. 48. **तार्क्ष्यो यदर्थ**— This third instance is not as strong as the first two. In killing serpents Garuda was simply following the course of nature (जीवो जीवस्य जीवनम्। Mb. Śântip). तृणमिव– This is used when a person sets very small or no value on & thing. Jimitavahana's magnanimity lies in this that he holds life so cheap, while the rest of the world cannot do it. cf तृणमिव वने शून्ये त्यक्ता न चाप्यनुशोचिता Uttar. III. 32. तृणमिव लघुलक्ष्मीर्नैव तान्संरुणद्धि। Bh. Nit., राज्यं येन पदान्तलग्नतृणवत्त्यक्तं गुरोराज्ञया। &c.

 P. 85. व्यवसाय—determination; for a slightly different meaning cf. supra p. 44 निर्व्याजा— निर्गतो व्याजः यस्याः; without any deceit about it; sincere (read guileless for guiltless in the trans.). **निर्बन्ध**— persistence. परार्थं—For the benefit of others **बद्धकक्षाणां**— Who have girdled their loins, i. e., determined always to make a strenuous effort for. **परार्थदत्तदेहानां** v.l., who have given up their bodies to the cause of others, i.e., taken off their ममत्व over their bodies. This reading is perhaps preferable as better agreeing with the Hero's words at p. 9, मया हि शरीरतः प्रभृति &c. The gist of the Śl. is-you should therefore leave an insignificant being like myself to die, and save a life so noble as yours.

 P. 86. **अध्यवसायः**—Determination, firm resolve; this refers to the Hero's words कर्मणैव हि सम्पादयामि &c.; see *supra* p. 83. **अन्तरायः** – Lit., what comes between (अन्तः + अय् to go ); hence, an obstacle.** विकल्प**— optionality of thought; hence hesitation. **शङ्खधवलं**— A comparison that would suit in the mouth of Sankara alone. शङ्ख is put in merely for alliteration with शङ्खचूड and शङ्खपाल. Cf. the comic verse अस्थिवद्वधिवच्चैव शङ्खवद्वकवत्तथा। &c. शङ्खपालकुलं —शङ्खपाल is one of the eight principal Nágas; cf. अनन्तं वासुकिं शेषं पद्मनाभं च कम्बलम्। धृतराष्ट्रं शङ्खपाल तक्षकं कालियं तथा । where अनन्त and शेष are the same. *(Navanâga*– stotra). **अथानुकम्पनीयाः**— Here अथ has the force of But if'; cf अथ मरणमवश्यमेव जन्तोः। Veni. III. C. अथ गृह्णाति S'ak. VII. त्वदायत्तः—In your power; lit., deponding upon you (your will); it rests with you . दैवायत्तं कुले जन्म मदायत्तं तु पौरुषम् । Veṇî. III. 37. भाग्यायत्तमतः परम्। Śâk. IV. 17.

 P. 87. **जननीं पुरस्कृत्य** — Taking your mother with you; lit., placing her in the front (out of respect); cf. पुरस्कृता वर्त्मनि पार्थिवेन । Rag. II. 20; वसिष्ठाधिष्ठिता देव्यो गता राघवमातरः । अरुन्धतीं पुरस्कृत्य यज्ञे जामातुराश्रमम् ॥ Uttar. I. 3. स्त्रीस्वभावकातरता—timidity or nervousness natural to women. कङ्काल—A skoleton; कं happiness, or कं head, कालयति (dissipatus) इति; fr. कल् + अच्. The comp. should rather have beon विपन्नानेकपन्नगकङ्काल &c.श्मशानं—श्मानः शवाः शेरते अत्र; & comp. of the पृषोदरादि class. चञ्चत &c.—In this Sl. the poet dolineates the बीभत्स रस or sentiment of disgust, with a shadu of the Terrible (रोद्ररस); जुगुप्सा or aversion is ils principal mood. Stinking tlesh, fat &e. are its आलम्बनविभावः or substantial excitants; the presenc of hideous birds &c. are the enhancing excitants (उद्दीपनविभावऽ). The poet's delinoation of this Rasa is far inferior to that of Bhavabhuti for which see Mâl. —Mâd. V. The description here is greatly exaggerated; and it is hard evon for the oriental mind to conceive how such a great stream of marrow and blood could have been flowing there, although the poet calls the cemetery a महाश्मशान, as no great city is mentioned as existing in its neighbourhood. The cometery hero spoken of is the vast forost-tract round the बध्यशिला referred to above. Garuḍa, as is the habit of birds, seized his victim and flew to some part of the forest to fenst upon him, leaving cach time a skeleton there. In the fifth act wo are told that Garuda flew with Jîmûtavâhana to a summit of the Malaya mountain. चञ्चत्—Moving about, as they (tho vultures) nibbled off pieces of flash Some take the चञ्चग्र to refer to Garuḍa, but that does not seem possible, as Garuda was not then feeding on any serpent, and so चञ्चत् cannot refer to his beak. The पिशितलबऽ were probably those dropped about as Garuda cut off flesh from his victim's huge body, as also those that remained sticking to the skeleton after it was left there by him. (Cf. the next verse प्रतिदिनमशून्यमहिना). As soon as Garuḍa finished his meal and departed, these carrion-birds gathered there and feasted on the remnants of flesh, When the vultures seized the pieces of flesh and flew up, parts of them dropped down as they closed their beaks, and the greedy creatures dartod down to catch them again. The reading **चञ्चूधृतार्धच्युत** means ‘the parts of the pieces of flesh held in their beaks that are dropping down in the middle.' Here the word is **चञ्चू **S'ivaráma reads **चञ्चूद्धृतार्ध॰** which he explains as **चञ्चन्त्या चञच्वा उद्धृतादर्थादंशात् च्युतस्य उद्धृतादर्धच्युतस्य वा। अर्धमार्गे व्यावर्तते इतिवत् अर्धपथे च्युतस्य वा। चञ्चूचाञ्चल्येन भ्रष्टस्य पिशितलवस्य ग्रासे इ॰।** **गृध्रैः** &c.—*cf*. **गृध्रैराबद्धचक्रं वियति विचलिते दीर्घनिष्कम्पपक्षैर्धूमैर्धर्वस्तार्कभासां सघनमिव दिशां मण्डलं दर्शयन्तः। **Mud. III.

 ** वक्त्रोद्वान्ताः** &c.—The reading of this line here adopted from the Triv. ed. is the best that is available. Some jackals are described as **उल्कामुख**s, *i. e.,* emitting flames of fire from their mouths (see Mál.-Mad. V. 13, where Jagaddhara gives शृगालभेदाः as an optional meaning of **उल्कामुख**). As these flames came in contact with the stream of blood they merged into it with the sound **छिम्** and got extinguished; see com. The reading **शमितशिखिशिखा॰** makes the meaning obscure. In this case the construction is **अस्मिन् श्मशाने शिवानां वक्त्रोद्वान्ताः ०विस्त्रे आस्त्रस्रोतसि पतन्त्यः अत एव शमिताश्च ताः शिखिशिखाश्रेणयः श्च ताः स्वनन्ति।** In which the rows of the flames of fire of the female jackals that are extinguished as they fall in the stream of blood......being vomited forth from the mouths of female jackals, are making a sound. The reading **यत्रोद्दामं भ्रमन्त्यः शमित (स्थगित) शिखिशिखाः श्रेणयः** &c. means–where the rows of female jackals, wandering at will (lit. unchecked) with the flames of fire (emitted from their mouths) extinguished (by the stream) are howling in the stream &c. But this, as remarked by Messrs B. and P. looks like an emendation of some editor; for here **यत्र ** does not agree well with **अस्मिन् अजस्र—न जस्यति** (which leaves no break; **जसिर्नञ्पूर्वः क्रियासातत्ये** **वर्तते।** Sid.—Kam) fr. **जस्** to set free 4th Conj. with the negative particlo prefixed, and aff. **र** which is added to denote babit **(ताच्छील्ये)** to roots **नम्, कम्प्,** and other; so **नम्, कम्प्र, स्मेर** &c see Páṇ. III. 2. 167. **वसा**—fat. **विस्र**—stinking of raw and stale flesh.

 **P. 88. प्रतिदिनं** &c.—In this S'I the cemetery is described as resembling the body of S ́iva by means of expressions common to both **श्मशान** and **वपुः** Thus **अहिनाहारेण**—means (1) **अहिना आहारेण** (not void of) a serpent sorving as food to Garuḍa; (2) **अहिना** **हारेण** are of a serpent forming the necklace of. S ́iva is described as wearing serpents as ornaments on his body;

*cf*. **करेण शम्भोर्वलयीकृताहिना ।** Kum. V. 66; **यथाप्रदेशं भुजगेश्वराणां करिष्यतामाभरणान्तरत्वम्** *Ibid*. VII. 34. For a similar expression yeilding **हार** and **आहार,** comp. **स्तनयुगमश्रुस्नातं समीपतरवर्ति हृदयशोकाग्नेः । चरति विमुक्ताहारं व्रतमिव भवतो रिपुस्त्रीणाम्**॥Kád. I.

 **विनायकाहित॰**—(1) **वीनां नायकस्य** (see com.) **विनायके वा आहिता प्रीतिर्येन** which has produed a liking in the mind of the lord of birds; or **विनायकस्य आहिता प्रीतिर्यत्र** on which Garuḍa has fixed his affection; or where Garuḍa the enemy of the serpentrace (see com.) delights to be; (2) **विनायकेनाहिता प्रीतिर्यस्य** to which Gajánana brings delight; or **विनायकस्याहिता प्रीतिर्यत्र** on which Viná. has fixed his affection; **विनायकस्याहिता प्रीतिर्येन** which produces delight in Vináyaka. **शशिधवला॰**— (1) see com.; (2) wearing the moon, white bones and skulls or white bones and skulls lit up by (shining in the light of) the moon.

 **सामोपन्यासैः—** साम्नः उपन्यासास्तैः conciliatory proposals or speeches. He refers to the Hero's words **कुमार शङ्खचूड न मे** &c. p. 86. and s'l. 17. **उपन्यास** is lit, what is placed before one for consideration, &c.; *cf*. **अहो उपन्यासशुद्धिः।** Mâl –Mád. III. p. 69; hence a proposal about &c. **त्रासोपन्यासैः**—*v.l*. means talking about or mentioning things inspiring fear or calculated to strike terror, referring to the fearful aspect of the cemetery. But the word **उपन्यास** does not fit in well with **त्रास**, as neither intended to strike terror into the other. The Calcutta editions read **नायकः—शङ्खचूड तद्गच्छ** &c. assigning the speech from **आसन्नः खलु** &c. to S'aṅkhachûḍa. But the word **अपि **used after **त्वं** by S'aṇkhachúḍa shows that he must have asked some other person to go away before he requested his mother to do so, and hence the speech **तद्गच्छ **&c. ought also to form part of S'aṅkhachúḍa's speech.

 **गतौ— **birth or species of life. **प्रियसुता**—sec com.; also **सुतप्रिया,** &s **प्रिय** optionally takes **परनिपात** (comes second) in & Bah. comp. **माता भूयाः** &c.—this virtually means that he should have the good fortune to be born as son her alone. Compare the similar wish expressed by Makaranda—**प्रियस्य सुहृदो यत्र मम तत्रैव सम्भवः । भूयादमुष्य भूयोपि भूयासमनुसञ्चरः॥** Mal.—Mád. IX. 41. It is difficult to see why **शङ्ख॰** speaks about himself in the plural.

 **अपश्चिमं—**Lit., that after which there is to be no other, *i. e.*, which is the last; means the same as **पश्चिमं** (which the Triv, Ed. reads); *cf.* **अयमत्र ते जन्मन्यपश्चिमः पश्चिमावस्थाप्रार्थितो मकरन्दबाहुपरिष्वङ्गः।** Mâl. Mâd. IX.; and **तात अम्बायं मे पश्चिमः प्रणामः** *infra*. p. 118. Compare the similar use of the word which means the samething as **उत्तम.**

 ** P. 89.** **यावदहमपि** &c.—This speech of S'aṅkha. comes on rather abruptly after that of his mother in which she expresses her resolve to die along with him. For, we should naturally expect S'aṅkha. to say something by way of dissuading her from such a course; but he does not do that. The Triv. Ed. reads the last part of the preceding speech, as **तत्त्वया सह गमिष्यामि;** but this also does not help us out of the difficulty.

 **यावदहमपि**— Some read **अस्मादुत्तरेणादूरे** where the abl. is ungramatical. For by the *sûtra* एनपा द्वितीया Pâṇ. II. 3. 31, words indicative of direction formed by the affix **एन (एनप्)** govern either the acc. or the gen., and not the ablative. The line **तत्रागारं धनपतिगृहादुत्तरेणास्मदीयं** (Meg. II. 15) oan not be cited in support of the abl.; for commenting on it, Malli. himself adopts the reading **गृहानुत्तरेण,** though he finds some defence for the viriant **गृहाद्;** see his com.

 **दक्षिण॰**—** गोकर्ण** is the name of a place which lies 5 miles south-east of the Gangavali river, close to the sandy shore, in the Canara District, and which is the site of a temple of S'iva, of great celebrity and popularly known as **गोकर्णमहाबळेश्वर.** *Cf*. **श्रितगोकर्णनिकेतमीश्वरम्।** Rag. VIII. 33. Here it is used for the liṅga itself (which is said to be of the form of a cow's ear). It is called **दक्षिणगोकर्ण **because it is in Southern India, but more probably for alliteration with **प्रदक्षिणकृत्य**. For in the Kathâ. or Bb.-M., the simple name **गोकर्ण** is used. We have already seen the poet's fondness for alliteration. *Cf*. *supra* note on **शङ्खधवलं**. Messrs B. and P. say it is one of the 12 Jyotirliṅgas (Intro. p. xxvi) and it is called *Dakshina* to distinguish it from the northern one in Nepal. But we do not find the name of Gokarṇa among the 12 Jyotirliṅgas mentioned in the S'iv.-P. or in the Jyotirliṅga-Stotra. **प्रदक्षिणीकृत्य**— going round the *liṅga* or the shrine in such & way as to keep it to the right side, as a mark of reverence.

 **कष्टं न सम्पन्नं** &c.—He did not gain his object as he did not get the pair of red garments, without which Garuḍa could not have eaten him. The reading **नाय॰–सम्पन्नं मे** &c. will not do as it leaves no room for the next portion, **तत्को नामा॰**.

 **इदं रक्तांशुकयुगलं**— While the Hero is thinking of how he should achieve his object, the Kañchukin unexpectedly enters and wishing to offer the garments sent by Mitrávasu's mother begins his speech by saying **इदं** &c. This portion of the Kañch's unfinished speech is so introduced as to be at once taken in connexion with the query **तत्को नाम** &c. and understood as an answer to that. This is technically called Patákásthána. According to S.-D. (VI. 48) this is the third kind of Patákásthána. For another instance see infra p. 95, and notes.

 **देव्या मिनायसुजनन्या** &c.— is to be read with the preceding **इदं रक्तांशुकयुगलं.** It is rather strange that the Kañchukin should hand over the garments to the prince in the cemetery, instead of leaving them with his parents. In the first place it is difficult to understand how the Kañch, directed his steps to the cemetery. We see from the *Vishkambhaka* to the present act that the Kañchukin had approved of the Pratîhára's suggestion to go to the Princess who then stayed with her father-in-law, and we should expect him naturally to go there, which how-ever he does not appear to have done. It was necessary for the further development of the plot to furnish the Hero with red garments at the proper time and the poet manages to do it somehow.

 **सफलीभूतः** &c.— Because he got the red garments owing to the marriage custom, at a time when he badly wanted them; for these could serve as the emblems of a victim. The garments serve a different purpose under different circumstances in Mṛich.; *cf*. **रक्तं तदेव वरवस्त्रमियं च माला कान्तागमेन हि वरस्य यथा विभाति।** X. 34. **मद्वचनात्—मद्वचनमिति कृत्वा। ल्यब्लोवे पञ्चमी।** Malli. on Rag. XIV. 61; speaking for me; in my name; *cf*. **तां चायुष्मन्मम च वचनात्** &c. Meg. II. 41.

 ** P. 90.** **परार्थे** &c.— **परार्थैकदृशो मम** *v. l*. means (1) **परार्थ एव एकः मुख्यः तत्र द्वयं यस्य** whose eye is directed only to another's interest; or (2) **परार्थे एका दृष्टिर्यस्य** whose eye is solely directed to another's interest.

 **चलित॰—** occasioning the shaking of &c., see com.; 'which has shaken &c.' is not an accurate translation as that will require **चालित** in the text.

 **संवर्तकाभ्रैः—** These are a class of clouds (one of the four mentioned in the com.) which pour their inexhaustible stores at the destruction-time of the world and produce a deluge. **पक्षतीनां—पक्षति** means 'the root of a wing', **ति** is added to **पक्ष** in this sense by **'पक्षात्तिः,**' Pâṇ. V. 2. 25. Here it is used for the quill feathers which grow in rows and form the wing.

 **कल्पान्त॰—** **कल्प** is a day of Brahman, equal to the four Yugas rolling over a thousand times (*i. e.*, covering a period of 4,320,000,000 solar sidereal years) which is also the time of the duration of the world; the night or the interval between the destruction and the re-creation of the world is also of the same length. **उद्यान्त**—shining lustre; refulgence. **कपिशयति**—Because Garuḍa has a body of a golden complexion. **मुहुर्द्वादशा॰**—The Triv. Ed. reads **शिशुद्वादशा॰** which the Com. S'ivarâma explains as **शिशुरल्पा द्वादशादित्यानी प्रलये समुदितानां समुच्चिता दीप्तिर्येन। ततोप्यधिक इत्यर्थः।** But this is twisting the meaning of the word **शिशु** Nor can the comp. be explained as **शिशूनां** **उदितमात्राणां द्वादशादित्यानां दीप्ति इव दीप्तिर्यस्य,** as the comparison then becomes meaningless. Compare with the description here that of the advent of Jatáyu, Aruṇa's son, in Mv. **पर्यायक्षणदृष्टनष्टककुभः संवर्तविस्तारयीर्नीहारीकृतमेघमोचितधुतव्यक्तस्फुरद्विद्युतः। आरात्कीर्णकणात्कणाकृतगुरुग्रावोच्चयश्रेणयः शैनेयस्य बृहत्पतत्रधुतयः प्रख्यापयन्त्यागमम्॥** V. 1.

 **P. 91.** **मन्ये**— The variant **मनः** violates the metre. **मलयचन्दन॰**—Because that is the best. **अभिवाञ्छितार्थ॰**—This explains why the touch of the **वध्यशिला** gladdened him. The one thought that dominated his mind then was to do good to others. He lived for that and that alone. So any thing calculated to bring that about would please him.**स्पृष्टा**— as also **आश्लिष्टा** *v. l*. is to be construed with **मलयवती** as well as with **शिला.**

 **शयितेन** &c— This shows that the happiness he derived from lying in his mother's lap was to him greater than that derived from Malayávatî's embrace. **दृष्ट्वा** &c.—As Garuḍa descended from the sky he saw in the distance the disc of the moon; this put him in mind of the form of S'esha coiled into a circle through terror at his sight when he used to visit Pâtâla for devouring the Nâgas. **क्षिप्त्वा**—*V. L*. for **दृष्ट्वा** means—having cast aside, or discarded in scorn. संहरन्—causing to contract for **संस्नरन्** is not a good reading; for it is not possible for Garuḍa to see **शेष** in the sky.

 **सानन्दं**— Because it proved the might of his brother. **०विचलिते**— As the horses took fright and shied, they gave a jerk to the chariot causing the sun to shake thereby. **अपसर्पत्** moving away from. As Garuḍa flew through the clouds they receded from his extended wings, appearing to a looker-on from a distance to extend them yet further. The reading **अवसज्जत्** will not do, as the clouds could not have remained sticking to the ends of his wings. **महीत्रं—महीं धरतीति** fr. **धृ+अ (कः) गृध्नु—गृध्यतीति तच्छीलः** fr. **गृध्+नु (क्नुः)** by **त्रसिगृधिधृषिक्षिपेः क्नुः।** Pâṇ, III, 2. 140; 80 **त्रस्नु, धृष्णु,** and **क्षिप्नु.**

 Here Garuḍa is described as having seen the moon, crossed the sun and passed through the clouds in his flight from heaven to mount Malaya. Now properly spenking he ought to have seen the sun first, as it is was nearer to him than tho moon in his downward passage. Here two explanations are possible. The poet, although he knew that the sun was considerably at a greater distance from the earth than the moon. followed the popular notion that the moon was more distant than the sun (*cf.* the verse **गिरौ कलापी गगने पयोदा लक्षान्तरेऽर्केश्च जलेषु पद्म। इन्दुर्द्विलक्षे कुमुदस्य बन्धुर्यो यस्य मित्रं न हि तस्य दूरम्॥),** as he did that of making the sun drive in a chariot. Or, and which is more probable, the poet may not be taken as going against his knowledge of the relative distances of the planets. That day was the first day of Kártika, (see *supra* p. 72, **अस्मिन्दीपप्रति॰**, where the reading of the Triv. Ed., *viz*., **अस्मिन्दिवसे प्रति॰** corroborates our supposition; and Introd., Time-Analysis) when the moon was present in the sky along with the sun for almost the whole day. Now Garuḍa as soon as he came to the sun, saw also the moon further towards the earth. The cons. is **सानन्दमग्रजेन दृष्टः** (a past action) **अहं हिमांशोः बिम्बं दृष्ट्वा शेषमूर्तिं संस्मरन्** (a present action) **एष वेलामहीध्रं प्राप्तः।**

 **P. 92.** **पन्नगः**— a serpent, **पन्नं पतितं यथा तथा गच्छति इति,** fr. **पन्न+गम्+अ** (**डः**. *i. e.,* **अ** before which the **अम्** of **गम्** is dropped) by the Vártika **सर्वत्रपन्नयोरुपसङ्ख्यानम्।** so **सर्वत्रग** also.

 **भवे भवे**—In each succeeding birth. **एवमेव** &c.—There is nothing strange in Jîmúta's wishing to be born again and again if only his body can be of service to others; for birth solely for doing good to others is more covetable than simple Nirvâṇa in his estimation. The question, with persons truly bonevolent, is not who is saved; we have similar instances in king S'ibi's offering his flesh to save a bird or Dilîpa's offering his body to save Vasishṭha's cow.

 **निपतितं**— Lying motionlessly or steadily and not restlessly like the other Nâgas. **शेषानहीन्** &c.— From this it appears that the punishment for the breach of the agreement was whole-sale slaughter of the Nágas. Here we have the *Bîja* of the principal event of the next Act, *viz*., the saving of the Nâga race by the Hero. **अशनिदण्ड॰**— The compound must be taken as a Karm. (see com.) **तर** signifying mere excess; **चण्डतर** means 'very hard', and the meaning is—with a beak extremely hard like the thunder-bolt (and not 'harder than' &c., though the poet might have intended it in that sense).  
** दिग्धं** &c.— By an Utprekshâ he fancies that the victim was not covered with red garments, but with his own blood, as it were, gushing from his heart split open through his fear. *Cf*. **जयत्युपेन्द्रः स चकार दूरतो बिभित्सया यः क्षणलब्धलक्षया। दृशैव कोपारुणया रिपोरुरः स्वयं भयाद्भिन्नमिवास्रपाटलम्॥** Kâd. Intro s ́lokas.

 ** नेपथ्ये दुन्दुभिध्वनिः** &c.—The stage-direction **नेपथ्ये** is used simply to show that the drums were sounded by, and the flowers fell from, unseen hands. Or better read **नेपथ्यात्** as the Triv. Ed. does. Whenever any act of extraordinary benevolence, valour, &c. is done a shower of flowers is represented as falling from heaven, sometimes accompanied by sounds of drums; *cf*. Rag. II. 60; **श्रिया जुष्टं दिव्यैः सपटहरवैरन्वितं पुष्पवर्षैः** &c. S'is'. XX. 79.

** आमोद॰**— extremely sweet fragrance.

 ** P. 93.** **आ ज्ञातं** &c.— Garuḍa, ignorant of the true fact. accounts for the shower of flowers by supposing that it came from the Pârijáta in heaven being violently shaken by the wind arising from his velocity and thinks that the drum-like sound he heard was nothing but the rumbling of the Saṃvartaka clouds apprehensive of the destruction of the world. **कवलयन्**— means here ‘seizing by the beak.'

 **नागानां रक्षिता** &c. — This verse has two meanings, one **वाच्य** or applicable to the present case, the other **व्यङ्ग्य** or suggesting the subject-matter of the next Аct, bу **अभिधामूलकशाब्दीव्यञ्जना.**

 **गुरुः**— (1) heavy, having profuse flesh and blood in his body. **आकाङ्क्षा**— desire to eat. He means—on account of the abundance of flesh and blood in his body, I shall have my desire to eat serpents entirely satified *i. e.* I shall eat his flesh to my satisfaction to-day.

 In the second case **गुरु **means 'adviser, preceptor,' and **आकाङ्क्षा** doubts as to whether it is good to eat serpents or not. He means—instinctively feel that this protector of serpents will be my adviser and entirely remove my desire to eat serpents making me thereby take to **अहिंसा.** Here we have the fourth kind of **पताकास्थान** which is defined as **द्व्यर्थो वचनविन्यासो यत्र स्यात्काव्ययोजितः। उपन्याससुयुक्तश्च तच्चतुर्थमुदाहृतम्॥** S–D. VI. This is the sprouting of the seed cast in s'l. 26 *supra*.

 ** P. 94.** **प्रतीहार —**see *supra* p. 76. **स्वगृहोद्यान॰**— this is a general statement. When a person whom one loves **(स्निग्ध)** is absent, even though he might have gone merely for a stroll in his garden, one feels anxions about his safety, owing to one's affection **(स्रेह)** for him. If, therefore, when one knows him to have gone to a forest, and that too beset with many dangers, one's anxiety for him would be very great indeed. The prolonged absence of Jîmútaváhana, therefore, is a source of anxiety to his father-in-law; *cf.* **अतिस्नेहः पापशङ्की** S ́âk. IV. **किमु**– *i. e*., **किमु वक्तव्यम्। दृष्टबह्वपाय॰**—qualifies **स्निग्धे** supplied from the first line; ‘when he is in the midst of a forest which is dangerous **(प्रतिभय)** as it is known to be full of many mishaps **(अपाय)** (to the casual visitor).' **अपाय**—*c. f. * **भवत्यपाये परिमोहिनी मतिः** Kir. XIV. 19. **प्रतिभय** *adj*. full of fears, dangerous' (**भयङ्करं प्रतिभयं** Ak. I. 6. 20).

 **जलधि॰**— having a curiosity to see (1) tho sen-shore or (2) the tide flowing iu. **चिरयति**—tarries (in coming back home), Denom. fr. **चिर;** *cf*. supra, p. 20. **दुःखं**—*adj*. in a sorrowful mood.' **सन्निहित॰**—*adj*. to **उद्देशं** (*m*. a region). It is best to explain this as **सन्निहितः गरुडः तेन प्रतिभयं;** it is also equally correct to explain as **सन्निहितः गरुडः यत्र तञ्च तत्प्रतिभयं च.** Messrs B. and P. proposo to take **प्रतिभय** as a noun in the sense of fear' and to explain the comp. as **सन्निहितं गरुडात् प्रतिभयं यत्र,** on the plea that it is the fear, and not Garuḍa, that is 'always' present there. But to us this insertion of 'always' seems gratuitous as the text does not give **सदासन्निहित॰**, and there is no impropriety in describing Garuḍa as **सन्निहित,** when it was well known that he was present thore *every day* **(प्रतिदिनम् अहिपतीनिह भक्षयतिः पक्षिराजः** P. 75); and thus there is no need to strain the meaning of **प्रतिभय** and take it in a sense which, though authentic, is not so common.

 **शङ्कितः**— afraid **(शङ्का अस्य सञ्जाता). राजर्षिः**— Royal sage, one who being a king, had taken to the life an of ascetic **(राजा चासौ ऋषिश्व) उटज**—fr. **उट** *m*. leaves, grass etc. **(तृणपर्णादिः), उटाज्जायते इति.**

 **सहधर्मचारिणी**—is a familiar word for one's wedded wife, (also called **धर्मपत्नी**) as she ‘shares in all the husband's religious duties'; *cf*. **सह धर्म चरत इति प्राजापत्यः** A ́s ́valâyanagṛihya–S. I. 6.1. **उपास्यमानः**— attended upon, accompanied by.

 **क्षौमे** etc.— He describes Jîmûtaketu as he appears to hims comparing him to the ocean. **अयं जीमूतकेतुः तोयनिधेः** (genitive) **सुसदृशीं श्रियं धत्ते** 'has a beauty very similar to that of the ocean." The descriptive clauses are so worded as to be construed both with Jîmûtaketu and with the ocean, to sustain the simile**. क्षौमे** —*acc*. *dual* of **क्षौम**, a silken garment (so called because it was made of the fibres of a plant named **क्षुमा**)—object to **बहन्** The next three words describe the two silken garments that Jîm. wore. **भङ्गवती—** having folds; **तरङ्गिसदशे—** with their ends or hems **(दशा)** wavy or tremulous **(तराङ्गित); फेनाम्बुतुल्ये**—(and thus) resembling the waters (of the ocean) with foam (overspread on it). The **क्षौम**s resemble **फेनाम्बु,** because the latter is **भङ्गवत्** ‘with waves' and **तरङ्गितदश** ‘in a state in which its surface is always rippling. It will thus be seen that these two adjectives, though distinct, mean the same thing, as **भङ्ग** and **तरङ्ग** are synonyms. For this reason the roading **तरङ्गितचलत्फेनाम्बुतुल्ये** (where the whiteness of **फेनाम्बु** is similar to the whiteness of **क्षौम**s) is preferable. **तरङ्गितचलत्** (*wavy*, and hence rippling) corresponds to **भङ्गवत्. जाह्नव्येव** etc.—Just as the ocean has **जाह्नवी** (the river Ganges), Jîmûta. has his wife. The rivers are often spoken of as so many wives of the ocean; *cf*. **सरितो पतिः** Kum. II. 37. **देवी**—his wife. **सवयस्**—(1) of the same age as himself, **समानं वयः यस्याः,** when taken with the Queen; (2) full of aquatic birds (**वयस्**. *n*. a bird **सहिता वयोभिः**), when taken with the river. The variant **सुपयसा** means—having plenty of (1) milk, (2) water in it. But this is not appropriate in the case of the Queen who is old. **महापुण्या**—(1) having a great treasure of पुण्य; (महत् पुण्यं यस्याः gen. *cf*. **महान् बाहुः यस्य स महाबाहुः**), exceedingly holy; (2) greatly sanctifying **(महत् पुण्यं यस्याः** abl.); highly purifying. **महत्** becomes **महा** in a Bahuvrîhi comp. by **आन्महतः समानाधिकरणजातीययोः** Pân. VI. 3. 46.

 **P. 95. यस्य—जीमूतकेतोः अन्तिकवर्तिनी** being near (**अन्तिकं निकटे**—Medinî. **अन्तिक** *n*. vicinity) **मलयवती वेला यथा (=वेलेव) आभाति**—Malayavatî, who is near Jîmûtaketu, appears like the sea-beach, which is near the ocean. The likeness of Malayavatî to **वेला** is made manifest by the suggested sense of **मलयवती,** which, when understood with **वेला**, would mean having the Malaya mountains adjoining.'

 The Pratîhára first saw Malayavatî (looking like the Velá), beyond her the Queen (looking like Gaṅgâ joining the ocean), and then the King clad in white garments and having a well-proportioned body, and hence the simile.

 **विकीर्णम्**— 'spread' everywhere, expressing in one word the idea beautifully expanded by Kâlidâsa in **आरूढमद्रीनुदधीन्वितीर्णं भुजङ्गमानां वसतिं प्रविष्टम्। ऊर्ध्वं गतं यस्य न चानुबन्धि यशः परिच्छेत्तुमियत्तयाऽलम्॥** Ragh. VI. 77. **स्थिरधिया**— with a firm mind; by **काकाक्षिगोलकन्याय** this may be taken both with **स्थितं** and **चरितं सुसदृशान्वयजा**—born of a family in every way resembling our own (in wealth, nobility, etc.). For **अन्वय** *cf*. **सिद्धान्वयजा** *supra* p. 18.. **चिन्त्यो मया** &c. I have enjoyed everything, and performed all my duties as a king and as a householder; what now remains for me is to wait quietly for death, with a full consciousness of having fulfilled my mission in this world **(कृतार्थतया).** As explained in the com., Jîmûtaketu had achieved all the four **पुरुषार्थ**s, and was now ready to face death, whenever it would come, with an untroubled conscience.

 **जीमूतवाहनस्य**— This is the first word of a sentence which the **प्रतीहार** utters to explain his business (see next page **जीमूतवाहनस्य वार्तामन्वेष्ठं** &c.;) but before he completes it, he is suddenly interrupted by Jîmûtaketu, to whom the word **जीमूतवाहनस्य** seems immediately connected with his own word **मृत्युः**, and the sense **जीमूतवाहनस्य मृत्युः चिन्त्यः** at once comes to his mind (instead of his original one of **मया** **ममैव मृत्युश्चिन्त्यः**). The poet has deliberately used the word **जीमूतवाहनस्य** in immediate sequence to **मृत्युः** to create this effect, and also to hint prophetically at the coming events. This is technically called a Patâkâsthána, which is thus defined—"When instead of the thing thought of or expected, another of a like character is indicated by some unexpected circumstance-etc."; see com., next page; see also *supra* p. 89. This is a favourite device with Sanskrit poets and is found resorted to in several plays. *Cf*. **दुर्योधनः—अभ्यासितुं करभोरु ममोरुयुग्मम्॥ (प्रविश्य सम्भ्रान्तः) कञ्चुकी देव, भग्नम्।** which are the first words of the incomplete s'l. **भग्नं भीमेन भवतो मरुता रथकेतनम्** &c., but which coming after **ऊरुयुग्मम्** seem to mean something quite different and sinister. Venî. II. p. 47. For other instances see Uttar. I. p. 38; Màl.-Mádh. II. p. 52.

 **P. 96. कर्णौ विधाय**— as he could not bear to hear of his own son's death. **प्रतिहत॰**— see *supra* p. 84. **वृद्धा**—Jîmûtaketu's Queen-wife is meant; the student should not confound her with **शङ्खचूड**'s mother who was also called **वृद्धा** above, but she does not appear in this Act. The Triv. Ed, reads **देवी** throughout for **वृद्धा** in this Act, which seems to be better. **दुर्निमित्त**—The ominous sense Jîmútavábana's death' was understood by all except the door-keopor. **वामाक्षिस्पन्दनं**— the throbbing of the *left* eye in the case of males, and that of the *right* in the case of females, suggests something evil happening to one's self or one's relations in the near future. *Cf*. **अश्वत्थामा—(वामाक्षिस्पन्दनं सूचयित्वा। आः कथं ममापि नाम अश्वत्थाम्नः अनिमित्तानि समरगमनविघ्नमुत्पादयन्ति।** Veṇî. III. **भद्र**—'Good Sir! A term of address, **नियतम्**—Surely. **प्राणयात्रा**—“the sustaining of life'; **प्राणयात्रार्थं**—to search for and bring the means of livelihood **(कन्दमूलफलादि) आर्यपुत्र**—see p. 5. **अन्यदेव किमपि** *i. e,* some accident or mishap happening to him; the sentiment here is the same as in **स्वगृहोद्यानगतेऽपि स्निग्धे** *supra.*

* ** *****P. 97.** **आकूल**— distressed, confused. **स्फुरसि** etc.—addressing his left eye which has again been throbbing **अदक्षिण**—left; **न दक्षिणः** (right) **अदक्षिणः**; the meaning 'unkind' is also suggested, as its throbbing was inauspicions, **हतचक्षुः**—** **Voe. sing., “O you wretched eye.'**अयं भानुः**— “This sun', looking up towards the sky. **ते स्फुरितम् अपहतं** **करिष्यति**—will nullify the effect of your throbbing. As a Madras commentator explains, **सूर्यदर्शनन अशुभनिमित्तानि दूरीक्रियन्ते इति शास्त्रप्रसिद्धत्वादिति भावः सहस्रदीधितिः**— an epithet of the sun; *cf*. *supra* p. 25. **स्फुरन्**—with its throbbing lustre. The word is intentionally used to suggest the idea of one **स्फुरण** counteracting the effect of another **स्फुरण.**

 **आलोक्यमानं**— *se.* **एतत्** (line 4). **अतिलोचनदुःखदायि**— exceedingly painful to look at, because of its bloody appearance. **विमुञ्चत्**—giving out. **रक्तच्छटाः निजमरीचिरुचः** can be taken in three ways—(1) (dropping) streaks of blood (**छटा** f. mass), whose colour is the same as that of its own rays; (2) (emitting) red streaks of the lustre of its own rays (**०रुचः** being gen. sing.); (3) (sending forth) the lustre of its own rays, whose colour is red (**०रुचः** acc. plu., **रक्तच्छदाः** being explained as **रक्ता छटा यासां ताः).** We follow the first (see com.), because it is clear from the words **लग्नसरसमांसश्चूडामणिः** on the next page that the thing he saw was Jîmûtaváhana's crest-jewel with blood trickling down from it. **उत्पातवात॰** etc.—**उत्पात** means any portentous phenomenon causing serious disturbance of any of the five Mahábhûtas **(महाभूतविकारः)** such as an earthquake, &c. It is believed that at the time of an **उत्पात** violent hurricanes blow across the globe, causing tremendous confusion and damage; shooting stars or meteors also fall at such times,

 ** P. 98.** **लग्नसरसमांसः**—with flesh, from which blood is dripping **(सरस),** sticking to it; **सरस** *lit*, means 'moist, wet' and here by implication it should be understood to mean 'wet *with blood.*' **पुत्रस्येव**—Jîmútaváhana wore a चूडामणि, and naturally his mother in her over anxiety suspects that this might be her son's. **अपवार्य**—'aside', *i. e.*. intended to be heard by the **वृद्धा** only, and not by others. Note how the poet represents the daughter-in-law behaving modestly in the presence of elders. **मैवं भण**— do not say so; let us hope that it is *not* his. This speech should rather have been **स्वगतम्.**

 ** विक्लवः**—see p. 77. **अभूः**—Perhaps the King betrayed some sign of pain on hearing the Queen's suspicion; and hence the door-keeper's suggestion. He says this as some consolation to them, that they might not fall victims to grief prematurely. It is believed that serpents of the best species carry jewels on their heads; *cf*. **त्रस्तेन तार्क्ष्यात्किल कालियेन मणिं विसृष्टं यमुनौकसा यः। वक्षःस्थलव्यापिरुचं दधानः सकौस्तुभं ह्रेपयतीव कृष्णम्॥** Ragh. VI. 49. See Malli. on Kum. 1. 6 (**करीन्द्रजीमूत॰** &c.). **अनेकशः**—may be taken either with (1) **पतन्ति** or with (2) **उत्खाताः**, since Nâgas are described as possessing not only one, but often five, ten, or more heads. **नखमुखोत्खाताः**—torn off by Garuḍa's nails and beak. In the verse read here in the Triv. Ed. (sce foot-notes) **उल्कारूपाः** means 'resembling meteors'; *cf*. *supra* **उत्पातवाततरलीकृततारकाम** p. 97.

 **सोपपत्तिकं**— what stands to reason; **उपपत्ति**—reasoning, explanation, argument. **इयत्या वेलया** 'by this time', as it is so late. **अपि नाम**—'can it be that', let us hope that it is'; *cf*. our note on **अपि नाम** *supra* p. 67.

 **P. 99.** **ततः प्रविशति** &c.— The poet does not tell us how S'aṇkha. comes back alone, whether having succeeded in persuading his mother to go back or by using the miraculous power which the chief Nágas possessed of suddenly vanishing from view; *cf*. **नागराजस्ततो राजंस्तत्रैवान्तरधीयत।** Nalopákhyána. **मुषितः** 'robbed'; 'fate has robbed me'. S'aṇkha, blames his fate which did not allow him the credit of having dons his duty by offering himself to Garuḍa; for, by the time he returns from making his obeisance to Gokarṇa, he finds that Garuḍa has taken off Jîmûtavâhana, instead of himself, his proper victim.

 **गोकर्ण** etc.— **तां वध्यभूमिम्**. He uses the word **तां**, and not **एतां**, because he had left the **वध्यभूमि** and entered here, following the track of blood. Hence the reading **तामिह** is to be rejected *Cf*. **तदिति परोक्षे विजानीयात्**। H. S. Gr. § 136. **विद्याधरं—**Jîmûtavâhana.

 In this stanza Messrs. B. and P. understand **च** in a disjunctive sense, and translate it by 'but'; **अहं बध्यभूमिं प्राप्तः, गरुत्मान् गगनम् उत्त्पतितश्च,** I came, but Garuḍa has flown away with him'. It seems, however, that the **च** is here used to denote the simultaneous or undelayed occurrence of the two actions (**यौगपद्य** S ́ivaráma); 'no sooner did I come.....than Garuḍa......’ It is generally used together with a second **च** in the preceding clause (as in **ते च प्रापुरुदन्वन्तं बुबुधे चादिपूरुषः** Ragh. X. 6); but here we have only one **च** used loosely; or **खलु** in the first half may be understood to be filling the place of **च.** S ́aṅkhachûḍa must have gone there *just in time* to see Garuḍa lifting off Jîmûtavâhana; and thus in **नखमुखक्षतवक्षसं** he describes what he actually saw.

 **निष्कारणबान्धव**—‘a friend without a cause', *i. e,* a disinterested friend. **कारुणिक**—see note on the word, p. 1. **विपद्वारिनिधि॰** etc.— you who are a boat, as it were, to take in and save people who are fallen into the ocean of misery, and who would otherwise be drowned in it; **पोत** *m*. a boat. **परोपकारतृणीकृत**— see com.; *cf*. **प्राणांस्तानेष साधुस्तृणमिव कृपया यः परार्थं जहाति** *supra* p. 84. **प्रयच्छ मे प्रतिवचनं**— give me a reply (and thus assure me of your safety).

 **नाहित्राणात्** etc.— **एका कीर्तिः** 'excellent fame,' **एक** being taken in the sense of chief' (**एके मुख्यान्यकेवलाः** Ak. III. 3. 16). If he had offered himself as part of the protective measure adopted to save the Nágas **(अहित्राण),** he would have carned permanent fame as a martyr in the cause. **एकाहं,** *v. l*., means 'one day', *i. e,* on that particular day when he was to serve as Garuḍa's food; on the next day another would get that sort of fame, and so on.

 **नापि श्लाघ्या** etc.—For this **आज्ञा **see p. 79. **शोच्यः**—‘one to be pitied.’ He uses this epithet with reference to himself. because it was in his opinion a very ignoble thing that he should allow his own life to be saved by the sacrifice of another's; it was too selfish and mean—so the people would judge, **वञ्चितः**— 'deceived', *i. e,* by fate; *cf*. *supra* **मुषितोऽस्मि दैवेन.**

 P. 100. **एवंविधः**— *i.e* **शोच्यः,** as he described himself in the last verse. **उपहास्यं** For people would take him to be a coward shrinking from death and so treat him with contempt and ridicule. **नाहं **&c....**करोमि—**he means that he would follow the track of blood, and discovering Garuḍa by that means, would offer himself; ho does not wish to live a life stained by ignominy.

 **आदावुत्पीडपृथ्वीं** etc.— In this verse he describes the line of the blood of Garuḍa's victim, which he is following in order to come upon Garuḍa. The line is in the beginning thick because a large amount of blood gushed forth in a stream at first. Then it consisted merely of a few big drops fallen at intervals (from the sky, as the victim was rapidly carried through space). On rocks the falling drops were shattered into many minute spray-like specks of blood. On the bare ground ants and vermin, as is their habit, had occupied the line (blood being their food). In places abounding with red mineral dust, the line was almost invisible, as the redness of blood was not apparent there. On the leaves of treck the drops of blood had become congealed.

 **उत्पीडपृथ्वीं**— *scil*, **रक्तधाराम्**. **पृथ्वी** *fem*. of **पृथु** *adj*. large.' **उत्पीड** *m*. bursting out into a stream; cf. **नयनसलिलोत्पीडरुद्धावकाशां** Megh. II. 31 (where Malli, paraphrases **उत्पीड** by **प्रवृत्ति**). **आपातशीर्ण**०— As the blood fell on the stones. its stream was broken **(शीर्ण)** as it dashed against them, and small particles **(तनुकणऽ)** flew off **(प्रसृत)** from it in all directions. **स्थली**—*fem*. of **स्थल**, in the sense of ‘a natural piece of ground; the other fem. form **स्थला** means 'a piece of ground artificially prepared' by draining, raising &c. **धातुपीठ**—slab-like solid stretches of land abounding in red mineral ore. We have preferred the reading **घनतरुशिखेर गहरे** to **वनतरुशिखरे स्त्याननील॰** for two reasons: (1) In the first place it was not possible for S'aṅkha., walking on the ground, to see what was on the tops of the trees; (2) secondly there could not have been a line of the blood-drops on the tops of the isolated trees, as there could be on the tops of the trees in a cavern where they grow in a cluster and have their top branches thickly intermingled. **घनतरुशिखरे स्त्यान॰**— *v. l.* also will not do, as the top of a single tree although it may be **घन** can not have such an even surface as to have a lino on it. In our reading such a **गह्वर** is taken as is close-packed with trees. **स्त्यान**—p. p. p. of **स्त्यै** I. P. to mass together. Road **स्त्यानं** for **समानं** in the com, **निपुणं** *adv*., 'carefully'.

 **रुदितवदनः**—explain **रुदितं** (crying, lamentation) **बदने यस्य सः;** or to avoid a **व्यधिकरणबहु॰** we may explain **रुदितं** as **रुदितमस्पास्तीति रुदितं** by adding **अ** which is added to words of the **अर्शआदि** group, as in the case of **पीता गावः, भुक्ता ब्राह्मणाः** (see Mallinatha on **विदितः** Kir. I. 1) and take the comp. as **रुदितं बदनं यस्य. आकुलीकरोति**— he seemed to her to bring bad tidings.

 P. 101. **त्रिभुवनैकचूडामणे —** Mark the wording of the passage here. Śaṅkha, is lamenting for Jîmúta, who is figuratively called the one Chudamani (the best ornament) of the three worlds. But the word **चूडामणि** is understood literally by Jîmútaketu, who understands S'ańkha. as mourning the loss of his own gom. **मांसलोभात्**—this can be explained in two ways; (1) attracted by the flesh, i, e., mistaking it for flesh, because of its bright-red colour; cf. a similar mistake in **आमिशषङ्किना मृगेणाक्षिप्तः।** Vikr. V. p. 117. (2) to partake of the flesh which was already sticking to it' as the gem was **लग्नसरमांस** (p. 98). **हा परार्थदत्तदेह —** is omitted from this speech as going against the context; for the speech is so worded as to make Jimúta believe that the Nâga is in search of his crost-jowel only.

 **अविधवे**—O you who are 'not-a-widow, i. e, whose husband is alive (there is an implied blessing in this). The word is very old in Sanskrit literature; it is generally used in the voc., and in a context where the life of the husband is supposed to have been in danger, and then his safety is to be assured. Cf. **भर्तुर्मित्रं प्रियमविधवे** &c. Megh. II. 39 (**अविधवे इत्यनेन भर्तृजीवनसूचनाद‌निष्टाशङ्कां** **वारयति** Malli.) **ईदृशी आकृतिः** — Such a beautiful form as yours could not have been intended by fate to suffer widowhood; *cf.* **तादृशा आकृतिविशेषाश्चिरं दुःखभागिनो न भवन्ति।** Vik. IV. p. 95. **युष्माकं** etc. —as behoves a well-bred and modest daughter-in-law. Malayavatî attributes her good luck to the blessings of the olders. **बाप्पोपरुद्धकण्ठः**— *Cf*. **कण्ठः स्तम्भितबाष्पवृत्तिकलुषः** etc. Śâk. IV. 6; **निरुद्धबाष्पोदयसन्नकण्ठम् उवाच कृच्छ्रादिति राजपुत्री**। Kir. III. 38.

 **आवेदय**—tell; used with the gen. **मम** (*cf*. **राज्ञ आवेदयध्वं मां सम्प्राप्तं** Rámáyaṇa); it is moro commonly found with the dat. as in **सा किमावेद्यते तुम्यं** Kum. 6.21. See Apte's *Guide*, § 68. **मयि सङ्क्रान्तं**—transferred to me', for I shall be sharing it with you when you tell me about it. The idea that grief loses its poignancy when shared by others who are friendly, is common in literature; *cf.* **स्निग्धजनसंविभक्तं हि दुःखं सह्यवेद‌नं भवति** S'âk. III. p. 70. **कस्मे तावदेतं वृत्तान्तं निवेद्य सह्यवेदनमिव दुःखं कारयिष्यामि** P'riy. III.

 P. 102. **अवसरप्राप्तः— **diss. **अवसरं प्राप्तः** (Ace. Tatp. by **प्राप्तापन्ने च ।द्वितीयया** Pâṇ. II. 2.4), whose turn had come' (to become Garuḍa's food). The comp. could have also been **प्राप्तावसरः;** 800 H. S. Gram. §204 (a) **किं वा विस्तरेण**—He says that it would not do to give the story at great longth, as that would incan loss of time and the track of blood would be lost or become indistinct. **पद्धति**—track (fr. **पद् + हति**).

 **केनापि**— Some one, i, e., whose name or other parti- culars Śaṅkhahúḍa did not know.

 ** परहितव्यसनी**— Passionately devoted to the good of others. **ते पुत्रेण जीमूतवाहनेन** seil **संरक्षिताः प्राणाः**.

 **दुर्निमित्तं** — It does not appear from the context that there was any special ill omen to which Malayavatî could refer by ho**r में दुर्निमित्तं;** the word **मे **must, therefore, either (1) mean some omen which she experienced but which is not distinctly mentioned, as appears from her speech **अहं पुनरार्यपुत्रमप्रेक्षमाणा** &c. at p. 06, or (2) it might be loosely intended for 'ours' belonging to our party, as Jîmûtaketu's **वामाक्षिस्पन्दन** is alluded to on p. 97, which Malay, could understand as applicable to every one of them.

 **नूनं** etc.— till Jîmûta. mentioned it, S'ańkha. had no idon that they were relatives, or parents, of his benefactor; other- wise he would not have broken the news to them so bluntly and unceremoniously. **अय या विषधर॰—विषधर** lit. possessor of poison, also a general term for a Nága. The student will notice the play upon the word **विषधर** in its rudha (established by usage) and yangika (etymological) senses. **अहो प्राणप्रदस्य—** this is ironical, woll have I repaid the obligation conferred by Jîmûta' meaning that he has repaid it very ill, indeed, inasmuch as he has been the direct cause of causing pain to his benefactor's parents.

 P. 103. **गुरुजनशुश्रूषाभिज्ञ** — as the old father and mother well knew from personal experience. **पूडामणि** etc. When alivo Jîmútavâhana in his act of dutifully bowing down to the feet of his father caused his crest-gem to come in contact with them; now also it so happened that the **चूडामणि** foll down from the sky on his father's feet. This is pootically conceived as a deliberate act of the son, who, though in another world, wished still to salute his father in the usual way as it were. **विनय- क्रमः**— Here **क्रम** menus a proper course of action; *cf.* Bhása **द्रोणः—अयमक्रमः। दुर्योधनः— अथ कः क्रमः।** Pañchâritra I. **इदमनुचित मक्रमश्व पुंही** &c. Bh. St. 27. For a different meaning soo supra IV. 8. **एतावन्मात्रदर्शनः— '**who is visible only in this much, i. c., the only thing visible, which can be called a part of him, is this crest-jewel. Compare similar expressions as **कथाशेष, नामाविशेष, अस्थिशेष** (p. 120&c.

 ** शश्वत्**— always, regularly. **मसृणोपि** &०. The gem, being every day rubbed against his fest, had become smooth and glossy. But when Jîmûta. held it to his heart, it forcibly reminded him of his lost son, and exceedingly (**गाढं** ind. deeply) pained him (**विघट्टय्** to scratch, to piorco). Here the smooth jewel is inconsistently spoken of as proving hard, which is a rhetorical figure called **विरोध** (apparont inconsistency). The sonsations are due to Jîmûta's two states-whon he was alivo, and now that he is so no longer, also, the smoothness was a physical attribute, while the suggested hardness is a mental image only.

 P. 104. **वर्जयित्वा** — leaving out, excopt'; gerunds are often used with an adverbial force; *cf. supra* **केशान् विहाय** p. 69. **देहि मे चूडारत्नं—**She means that, in the absence of the body of her dead husband, she would mount the funeral pyre with that gem, as being a part of him or something belonging to him. **किं प्रतिपाल्यते—***cf* **दर्शनाबसर प्रतिपालयावः** p. 15; **प्रतिपालय क्षणं** p. 112. **आहिताग्नेः— **of one who, like Jimitaketu in the third (**वानप्रस्थ)** Asrama, had kept the three sacred fires, **गार्हपत्य, आहवनीय,** and **दक्षिण.** The comp. is usually **आहिताग्रि (आहिताः अग्नयः येन**); 300 Rag. II. 44. But it is one of a class of compounds whose members can change places; hence we can have **अग्न्याहित** also. See Páṇ. II. 2.37. About the keeping of the sacred fires, compare **बलीपलित संयुक्तस्तृतीयं तु समाश्रयेत्॥ गच्छेदेवं बनं प्राज्ञः स्वभार्यां सहचारिणीम्। गृहीत्वा चाग्निहोत्रं च होमं तत्र न हापयेत् ॥ कुर्याच्चैव पुरोडाशं वन्येैर्मेध्यैर्यथाविधि। भिक्षां च भिक्षवे दद्यात् शाकमूलफलानि च। कुर्यादध्ययनं नित्यम् अग्निहोत्रपरायणः।** Saṃvarta-Smṛiti, 97-100. No other fire except those of the Agnihotrin himself could be used for his cremation; *cf*. **आहिताग्रिर्यथान्यायं दग्धव्यस्त्रिभिरग्निभिः॥ अनाहिताग्रिर्ग्रह्येण लौकिकेनेतरो द्विजः।** Us'anas-Smṛiti, VIL. 6-7 **संस्कार**., the funeral rite, known as antyeshți. **अग्निहोत्रशरण—**the hall **(शरण** n. a place where the sacrificial fires are kept, **आत्मानं—**the reflexive pronoun **आत्मन्** is always used in *m*. sing., though the noun to which it refers be of any gender or number; *cf*. Rag. X. 60; see Apte's *guide*, § 140. Here it is *m. f*. in gender and plural in sense.

 **एवं तावत्**— he now means to dissuade them from their purpose by holding out some hope to them. **विधिविलसितानि — **the pastimes or sportive doings of fato; *cf*. **अहो दैवगतिश्चित्राः विधेर्विचित्राणि विचेष्टितानि** Subhá.

 P. 105. **दुर्लभं खलु**— The Horoine is naturally timid and is pessimistically doubting whether she could be so fortunate; the parents are more sanguine. **अवितथा—** true, **न** **वितथा; वितथ** adj. 'falso' (**विगतं तथा सत्यं यस्मात्**)

 **कर्माणः** etc.— In this s'l. S'aṅkha. describes Garuḍa as seen by him from a distance. **रुधिरार्द्र ०—**by scratching his beak against the rocks, as is the habit of birds of prey when eating, Garuda made doup pits in them; they looked like so many water- troughs (**द्रोणी** *f*) **कषण** rubbing; *cf.* **निकषण** *supra* s'1. 12. The student should notice the play of fancy leading to oxaggeration in this as well as in the next statement. **प्लुटो- पान्त**—By the successive flames (**शिखा श्चेणयः**) of the fire (**ज्योतिः** lit. lustre) proceeding from his eyes, he (Garuḍa) had burnt (**प्लुष्ट**) the interiors (**अन्तराणि**) of the adjoining forest **(उपान्त-वन) सज्जद्वज्र॰-** his nails, being much longer than his victim's body, came in hard contact with the earth, which they tore up as he moved him with them to one side or to another. The reading **सज्जद्वज्र"** is preferred to **मज्जद्वज्र** as Garuda was then merely holding the body of his victim with his claws. **नखरप्रान्त** the onds of the claws.

 P. 106. **प्रत्युत**— 'and more, on the contrary.' **प्रहृष्ट इव किमपि** v
I —In this case **किमपि** ought to be construed with **प्रहृष्टः.**

 **ग्लानिः**— etc. —He describes the signs by which he could see the quiet pleasure with which his victim treated his wounds, eto, **ग्लानिः—** 'exhaustion'; he is such a great tower of fortitude that although his blood is almost entirely drunk off, he shows no exhaustion, **मर्मासोत्कर्तनजा रुजः—**acc. plu., object of **बहतः; उत्कर्तन** n. tearing up, from **उद् + कृत्** 6 P. to cut. **गात्रं—** his limb; it can also be taken to mean body' here. **गार्च अने** **कलेबरे** *Medinî*. **न बिलुप्तं—** not disappeared (by being eaten up by me); *cf*. **विलुप्तशेषाङ्गतयां** *infra* s'I. 22. **पुलकः— **the hair of the body standing on end. This is occasioned by either **भीति** or **हर्ष**, but here it is due to the latter sentiment. The whole body of Jîmútaváhana had become **पुलकित** (horripilated) owing to his joy; but since a large portion of his skin had already disappeared, the **पुलक** was visible only on the remain- ing portion, **दृष्टिः** etc. Although I am doing him an injury, on me (**अपकारिणि मयि** loe. sing.) his eye rests with an expres- sion, not of fear or hatred, but of delight and gratitude, as though I am conforring some favour on him (**उपकारिणि इव मयि**). The mind (will-power) of the hero was so overpoweringly swayed by his desire to do good to others as to make his body quite insensible to pain.

 **कुतूहलं**—Garuda is curious to know the reason of such extraordinary behaviour in the very face death.

 **शिरामुखैः**—through the openings (lit. months, i. e, the places where they are out) of the veins of the body. **किं** **भक्षणात्त्वं** &c—. 'why then do you stop from cating?" Jîmûta. here urges Garuda to go on and finish his meal; such a request whets Garuda's curiosity and onhances his admiration. This s1. is quoted in the D.-R. as an illustration of **धीरोदात्त नायक** and further again as an iustance of **औदार्य (प्रियोक्त्याऽऽजीविताद्दानमो-दार्यं);** also quoted in the S.-D. as an instance of **दयावीर.**

 P. 107. **एवम् ऊर्जितं**— thus nobly; *cf*. **उपपत्तिमदूर्जिताश्रयं नृपमूचे बचनं वृकोदरः** Kir. II. 1 (where Malli. paraphrases **ऊर्जित** by उदार) **आवर्जितं**—takon, Garuḍa says-while I have taken blood by my beak from your heart, you on the other hand have taken (i. e., made captive, won to your side) *my heart itself* by thus displaying fortitude. While I could only take a part, you have taken the whole, and have thus proved yourself to be greater than your assailant (myself). It will be noted that Garuda's action was physically truo, while he is referring to that of Jîmütaváhana in a moral or spiritual sense. The poctical contrast of the two adde rhetorically to the effect of Garuḍa's speech.

 **विफलीकृतः**— Mark the magnanimity of heart underlying these words; he fears that his high ideal may not be fulfilled now. **अस्थाने एव—**' at a wrong place'; i. e., there was really no room for doubt he explains in the next s'l, how.

 P. 108. **आस्तां** etc. In this a'l. S'aṅkha, describes the various marks eto, on his own body from which Garuḍa ought to have recognized him as a Nága. **आस्तां स्वस्तिकलक्ष्म** **वक्षसि—** I have the *swastika* mark on the chest, but let it stand, let it pass (i. e., I will tell you of more). The **स्वस्तिक** is a mystical religious symbol of the Hindus denoting good luck. Accord- ing to some it was originally a symbol connected with sun-worship, but according to the late Sir. A. Cunningham, it represents a monogram or interlacing of the letters of the auspicious word **सु अस्ति (स्वस्ति)** in the As'oka characters. It appears that the Nagas had this mark on their bosom; even in our days we find a sort of figure on the hoods of cobras, though this is not exactly the Svastika mark. The Com. S'ivarâma takes the first line as referring to Jim., "let go the Svastika mark on his chest, no slough over his body is to be seen"; the Bṛihatk. mentions this mark on Jim.'s chest **(अस्मिन्नवसरे शङ्खचूडोऽभ्येत्य तमव्रवीत्। हा हा मा मा कृथास्तार्क्ष्य साहसं किं न पश्यासि॥ अस्य विद्याधरेन्द्रस्य स्वस्तिकाङ्कमुरस्तटम्।).** This explanation may be accepted on the authority of Kshemendra. But the general drift of the S'loka requires the line to be taken as referring to S'aṅkha., as we have done. If it bo urged that it will not be right to do so, as a serpent is not known to have the svastika mark, wo might as well reply that s serpent, as known to us, does not possess also three or more hoods, as stated in lines 3 and 4. It is obvions that the race of the Nagas to which S'ankha, belonged was not in every respect identical with the present-day snakes; secondly, it is not necessary for the mark to resemble a svastika exactly, to be called a svastika; thirdly, it was possible for Garuda to seo the mark on the person on S'aikha. alone, as he held up his bosom before him, while the bosom of the Hero was then pierced through and mangled. **नालोक्यते—** 'do you not see', i. e, you ought to have marked it. **कञ्चुक** **m.** the skin of a serpent, slough; *cf*. **भोगिनः कञ्चुकाविष्टाः** Pt. 1. 65. **जल्पत एव—** just as I spoko. **न गणिते नाम—**How possibly you omitted to count them? (**नाम** has the sense of **सम्भावना) तिस्रः फणाः**—The ancient Nâgas are described as having three, five, or even more hoods (S'esha, their King, has a thousand), and goms in them which shed their lustre all round; o०. **तत्फणामण्डलोदचिर्मणिद्योतित- विग्रहम् ।** Rag. X. 7. **तीव्र** **त्विषः** adj. *cf* **फणाः व्याजिल—**lit. distorted (*cf.* **व्याजिह्माङ्गाः कुरङ्गाः** p. 13), not proceeding straight, refracted and hence (their brilliance) dimmed by the mass (**पटल** n.) of smoke issuing from the fire of deadly poison, **दुःसह... स्फीताः** also adj. of **फणाः**. In his great agony he was breathing heavy sighs (**फूत्कृत**) which caused the hoods to expand still more. **स्फीत-**p. p. p. of **स्फाय्** I Â to increase, to expand **फूत्कृत—**the emitting of the sound *Phút*; hissing; an onomatopoetic word. Observe that in this verse Śaṅkha, enumeratos four marks distinguishing a Nigs from a Vidyadhara-the Svastika, the slough, the forked tongue, and the three- branched hood.

 **अकारुणिक**— Cruel, *cf.* **मिथ्याकारुणिक,** *supra* I. 1. **असौ—** *That* (Vidhyâdhara youth); **असौ** being connected with **यस्य** in the next s'loka.

 **मेरौ **etc.— Construe (**असौ जीमूतवाहनः यस्य तत् यशः बहुशः मया श्रुतम्।** Jîmûtavábana had already become so well-known from his benevolence that his fame had spread far and wide, and Garuḍa, who had neness overywhere, had heard it in all places. So he ruognises him at once by the name Jîmûtrahana **मेरौ—** Meru is a fabulous mountain in the centre of the earth, and wholly consisting of gold and gems. It is sometimes identified with the Himalayas. According to some it is the terrestrial North Pole, sos Arctic Home in the Vedas," pp. 67, 60 sec also impra 11. 13, note on **नंह, मन्दरकन्दरासु**— in the valloys (**कन्दर *m* कन्दरा** *f*
a valley) of the Mandara mountain The Mandara is the mountain which the gods used for charning the occan, it is supposed to bo a hill of that name in Blágalpur, which is held sacred. **महेन्द्राचले**—The Mabendra range is said to be identical with the northern part of the Gháts According to the Vishṇu, P. Meru and Himavat are **वर्षपर्वतऽ** while Mahendra and Malaya belong to the class of **कुलपर्वतऽ** ** प्रभार—m** the slope of a mountain; Mal Mada V. 19, IX. 13.

 P. 109. **लोकालोकविचारि**— traversing as far as the Lokáloka mountain (which is the furthest limit of all worlds); ie, filling the wholeuniverse; cf. Ragh. VI. 77 quoted at p. 78 (Notes); **कथं मम कारणात्समस्तलोकालोकान्तरालविख्यातनिर्मलकुलैकमङ्गलभूतमात्मानं** &c. Mál-Mádh. X. **विचार** is nout, sing qualifying **यशः**; it may also be taken as connected with **चारणगणेः,** the whole being one word,— by Châraṇas, who wander as far as the Lok. mountain. But the first way is better. The Lokâloka is a mythical range of mountains surrounding the son of fresh water, outermost of the seven seas, which itself surrounds **पुष्कर,** the last of the seven Dvipas, and dividing the visible world from the region of darkness. As the sun is within this wall of mountains, there is light within, and darkness without. **परेण पुष्करस्याथ आवृत्यावस्थितो महान्। स्वादकसमुद्रस्तु स समन्ताद्वेष्टयत्॥ **

** स्वादूदकस्य परितः शैलस्तु परिमण्डलः। प्रकाशश्चाप्रकाशश्च लोकालोकः स उच्यते॥** आलोकस्तत्र **चार्वाक्च निरालीकस्ततः परम्॥** Mât. P. Ad. 122 **लोक्यते इति लोकः** (light); **न लोक्यते इत्यलोकः** (darkness); **लोकश्च अलोकश्चात्र स्त इति, लोकश्चासौ अलोकश्च इति वा, लोकालोकः।** Malli. on Ragh. I. 68; *cf*. also **अन्तर्लोक्यते बहिश्च न लोक्यतेऽनर्कत्वात् लोकालोकः** । Kshîra, on Ak. II. 3. 2. **चारणगणैरुङ्गीयमानं—**sung by groups of Châraṇas, the heavenly bards whose duty it is to sing of the glorious deeds of gods or god-like heroes. *Cf*. **ततो वयमन्तरा चारणेभ्यस्त्वदीयं जयोदाहरणं श्रुत्वा** &c. Vik. I. p. 21**.**

 **अंहःपङ्के**—in the mud of sin; **अंहस्** n. sin. **उद्विग्न**—distrossed. **अस्थानं**—'not a proper place; he means that there was abundant reason why he should wear a distressed look.

 **स्वशरीरेण** etc— Śaṅkha, considered it below his honour to shirk the duty of sacrificing himself which was assigned to him, as well as to savo his own life at the cost of that of another person. He thought he would be consigned to hell for such heinous conduct, and Jîmútâvihana was instrumental in bringing it about. S'aṅkha. asks him is it proper for you to send me to hell? (or, proper indeed it is for you!) Construe **मदीयम् इदं शरीरं स्वशरीरेण ताक्ष्यान्त्परिरक्षतः भवतः** (gen. sing.) **मां पातालनलादपि तलं नतुं युक्तम् (किं, or युक्तमिदं).** Note that the root **नी** governs two accusatives. **पातालतलात् तलं** is a faulty expression; what is meant is **पातालतलात् अधस्तरं तले**—a place lower than Patâla. Patala is the region where the Nagas ordi- narily reside; below that, according to the ancient conception of the universe, is saraka or hell. **मद्रासगोचरपतितस्य**—'come within the range of being my food; about to become my prey. **अकृत्यं-अप्रशस्तं कृत्यं** an evil deed. **बोधिसत्त्वः** in his remorse Garuḍa calls Jimútavâhana a Bodhisattva on account of his greatness, **बोधिसत्त्व** (lit. one whose essence is bodhi or perfect knowledge) in Buddhistic literature means a Buddhist saint who has only one birth to undergo before attaining to the rank of a supreme Buddha. *Cf*. 1. **बोधिसत्त्वचरित** p. 4. **व्यापादितः**— killed; p. p. p. of the causal of **पह** with **वि** and **आ** 'to perish. **महापातक** — a great sin. **प्रायश्चितं**—atonement. In the Hindu religion every sin has a corresponding Prayas'chitta assigned to it, and heinous sins have death. The word **प्रायश्चित्त** is derived from **माय +चित्तः** 'permanent or fixed thought," coming in by Pân. VI. I. 157 and the Vartika thereon **(पारस्करप्रभृतीनि च सञ्ज्ञायाम्। प्रायस्य चित्तिचित्तयोः ।).** The popular derivation is given in Hemadri as **प्रायो नाम तपः प्रोक्तं चित्तं निश्चय उच्यते। तपोनिश्चयसंयोगात्प्रायश्चित्तमितीर्यते॥ अमी केचिद्गृहीताग्नयः—** He means Jîmûtaketu and the others who now come into his view.

 P. 110. **धारय मां**— He does not want that his parents should see him in that half–eaton, mangled condition; other-wise they would receive a terrible shock and may even die.

 **आत्मीयः** etc.— It is true that Jîmútavána's action in taking pity on a follow-being in distress was highly laudable in a universal sense. His fathor urges, however, that Jîmútaváhana might have shown more discretion. He need not have shown consideration for his parents *as parents, because* relationship or otherwise is not allowed by the noble to influence them in the exercise of compassion. However, he ought to have reflected that by saving S'aṅkha, he saved one life, but destroyed four-*viz*, himself, his two parents, and his wife. And hence true wisdom would lie in not making such an illogical sacrifice. The arithmetic of Jîmûtaketu's argument is unanswerable; but it does not consider the selfishness that underlies it. Compare how in Ragh.II. 48, the Lion urges a similar half-truth upon Dilîpa's consideration—**भूतानुकम्पा तव वेदियं गौरेका भवेत्स्वस्तिमती त्वदन्ते। जीवन्पुनः शश्वदुपप्लवेभ्यः प्रजाः प्रजानाथ पितेव पासि॥ आत्मीयः** etc. **(अयं) आत्मीयः (अयं) परः इत्पयं क्रमः कृपायों कुतः खलु। सत्यम्।** For the sentiment in this line compare **अयं निजः परो वेति गणना लघुचेतसान्। उदारचरितानां तु वसुधैव कुटुम्बकम्॥** Pt. V. 38. **आत्मीयः**—lit. 'one's own', *i. e,* a relative, **क्रमः**— order. **बहवः**—*i. e,*, **आत्मा, पितरौ** and **वधूः** (line 4). **एकः**—*i. e,* **शङ्खचूडः**, **चिन्ता**—Consideration. **येन त्वया**—the corresponding antocedent to **येन** is **ते** in line 2. निःशेषं can be taken in two ways (1) adj. of कुलम्, or (2) adv. to हतम्; the ultimate sense is the same—of our family none will now be left behind.

 **अविरताश्रुधाराः**— in the com. read **अश्रुधाराश्व** for **ज्वालाश्चः विज्वालः**—gon. Bahuv.; **विगताः ज्वालाः यस्य सः,** 'whose flames have disappeared, *i. e,* extinguished. **अग्निः**— which they are carrying with them, *cf*. **अमी केचिद्गृहीताग्नयः** *&c.supra* p. 109.

 P. 111. **पर्याकुल**—troubled, in a fix. **तटस्थः**—is used here in the literal sense—'stand on the bank (or shore) of’ the ocean **(जलनिधेः)**; *flg.* it means standing aloof neutral'; *cf.* **तटस्थः स्वानर्थान्घटयति च मौनं च भजने** MâI.—Mâdh. I. 14. In N.-Ch. III. 55, the word is used in both these senses.

 **ज्वालाभङ्गैः **ete.— The constr. is **अस्मिन् वाडवाग्नौ पतामि,** the locatives **ईशे, धुक्षिते** and ०**भयङ्करे** being epithets descriptive of the **बाडवाग्नि**. Garuḍa, being on the shore, remembers the submarine fire in the sea and decides to immolate himself thetein, instead of socking fire elsewhere, or taking it from Jîmûtaketu. The existence of volennoes in mid-occan probably gave rise to the belief, common in Hindu mythology, in the existence of submarine fire. It is supposed never to be extinguished; on the contrary it helps to keep the ocean within its limits by consuming its surplus waters; at the end of a Kalpa it assists in the universal destruction. It is called **वाडव,** 'belonging to a mare' (fr. **वडवा.** f. a mare, a female horse), as it is supposed to be a personified being with the face of a horse; of **विदिद्युते वाडवजातवेदसः शिखाभिराश्लिष्ट इवाम्भसां निधिः।** S'is'. I. 20; also, Venî. V.19.

 **ज्वालाभङ्गैः**— Construe **सप्त समुद्रान् कबलीकर्तुम् ईशे; ज्वालाः भङ्गाः इव तेैः भङ्ग** *m.* a wave; by its wave like flames; or **ज्वालानां भङ्गाः,** the curling flames. **त्रिलाकी॰**— resembling the tips of the touguos of Kála, stretching out **(लसत्)** with the desire **(रस)** of swollowing **(ग्रसन)** the three worlds. Kâla is the God of Death, the spirit of Destruction personified, who destroys the worlds at the end of a Kalpa. **०जिह्वाग्रकल्पैः**— the affix **कल्प** is added in the sense of **ईषन्न्यून** ‘a little less than, 'almost equal to', like, resembling; *cf*. **ऋषिकल्पे राजनि** S'ák. II. **सप्त समुद्रान्**— the seas are stated to be seven in Hindu mythology, as consisting of **लवण, इक्षु, सुरा, घृत, दधि, क्षीर,** and **जल;** cf. **सप्तार्णवजलेशयम्** Ragh. X. 21; more usually their number is given as four, *cf*. **चतुरुदधिमालामेखलाया भुवो भर्ता** Kad. I. **कबलीकर्तु**— to make a monthful **(कबल)** of.

 **उत्पात॰**— (The winds or breezes produced by the flappings of his wings) which were swifter **(पटुतर)** in movement **(प्रसर** *m*.) than the hurricanes accompanying portentons phenomena **(उत्पात).** For **उत्पातवात** see note on **उत्पातवात** &c. *supra* p 97. **धुक्षित**—‘kindled', p. p. p. of **धुक्ष्** 1. Â. Caus. **कल्पावसान**— For Kalpa see p. 96; at the end of ench Kalpa the world is annihilated by terrible divine fires. *Cf*. **कल्पाग्निः पाण्डवानां द्रुपद**— **सुतचमूघस्मरो द्रौणिरस्मि** Venî, V. 37. **भयकर**—the word is more commonly mot with in the form **भयङ्कर.**

 **P. 112.** **अध्यवसाय** *m*.; see *supra* p. 86. **प्रतीकारः**—remedy, expiation, something that will make atonement for it. **दिष्ट्या वृध्**—*lit*. to prosper by reason of one's good fortune **(दिष्टि** *f.*);’ the idiom is often used in the sense of congratulating a person upon his (or her) good luck; *cf ***समाश्वसिहि कल्याणि दिष्ट्या वैदेहि वर्धसे।** Uttar. VII. 3. **ध्रियते**—is alive; fr. **धृ** 6 Â. *cf*. **ध्रुवं न सीता ध्रियते यथा न मे विचिन्वतो दर्शनमेति मैथिली** Rám. V. 12. 2. **ध्रिये आर्यपुत्र एषा ध्रिये।** Uttar, III. **पर्युपास्यमानः**—being waited upon. The idea here seems to be borrowed by the poet from Ragh, X. 13 **(उपस्थितं प्राञ्जलिना विनीतेन गरुत्मता).** **अक्षत**—not wounded, whole. **यत्सत्यं**— used adverbially in the sense of to tell the truth, as a matter of fact. **झटिति कृत्वा**— quickly; some indeclinables form compounds optionally with the gerund in **त्वा;** so we can have **झटितिकृत्य**— also. The words in the text, ought to have been printed separately as **झटिति कृत्वा** as they are not compounded. See H. S. Gr. §237. **न प्रत्येति**— does not feel confidence. This shows her extreme sensitivenoss.

 ** P. 113. वाङ्मात्रक** *n.*—mere words (even); **वागेव वाङ्मात्रम्** with the affix **क** added **स्वार्थे** **सम्भाविन**— honoured; *cf*. **त्वत्सम्भावितमात्मानं बहु मन्यामहे वयम्** Kum. VI. 20. **परात्मरक्षितजीव**— You who have saved your own life at the expense of that of another'. **गर्भस्थः एव**— *i. e.,* while unborn, **विपन्न**—dead; *cf*. *supra* p. 87 **(विपन्नपन्नगानेक॰** etc.) **मरणातिगं दुःखं**— grief (the agony of) which exceeds even that of death itself **नूशंसः**— **नृृन् शंसति हिंसतीति नृशंसः।** fr. **शंस्** to kill and aff. **(अ) असमीक्ष्यकारिता** thoughtlessness **(समीक्ष्य** having considered **करोतीति समीक्ष्यकारी, न भवतीत्यसमीक्ष्यकारी, तस्य भावः अ॰ कारिता). विजृम्भितं**— appearance, manifestation, consequence. **एवं तावत्करोमि**—*i. e,* before immolating himself he wishes first to restore the fainted persons by fanning them with his wings.

 **प्रत्युत्थितोपविष्टः**—recovered and sitting up; diss. **आदौ प्रत्युत्थितः पश्चादुपविष्टः** Karm. comp. **अमङ्गल्य** *adj*. **मङ्गले साधु मङ्गल्यं** fr. **मङ्गल+यत्। न मङ्गल्यमम॰ (अमङ्गलं** occurs just below); *cf*. अमङ्गल्यं शीलं तब भवतु नामैवमखिलं Mahimnaḥstotra. **ध्रियते**—See *supra* p. 112.

 ** P. 114.** **इयत्यां वेलायां**— after such a (long) time. बरं भर्तुस्ते मुखं दृष्टम्— *i. e.,* You might thank your good luck in so far that you could see your husband's face (at least). This is a half-hearted assurance, as they are not at all sure of his living, he being all mangled and torn. **विघ्नः**— This word which is *masc*, in Prâkrit becomes **विग्घं** *neuter*, which is its gender in the vernaculars,

 **विलुप्त**— His other limbs baving disappearod, being already eaten by Garuḍa, **निराश्रयत्वादिव**—as they had lost their substratum, **कण्ठ॰**—The life of Jîmût, was ebbing fast; he was in his last moments and the only sign of his life then was the breath passing in and out of the throat. Sometimes the meaning is metaphorical (as at IV. 11. p. 82). Construe **कण्ठदेशं प्रयातान् प्राणान्वहन्तं तनयं निरीक्ष्य** etc. **प्राण** is used in the plural, as the vital airs are supposed to be five. **कथं न पापः** &c.—He means— since I do not break off into a hundred pieces, I am a sinner *(i. e.*, destined to suffer prolonged grief). *Cf*. **दीर्ये किं न सहस्रधाहम्।** Uttar. VI. 40.

 **परामृशन्ती**—touching. **आभरणानामाप कृतशोभं**—So beautiful that when ornaments are put upon it it is the ornaments, and not his body, which appear brightened. The idea is the same as in **आभरणस्याभरणं प्रसाधनविधेः प्रसाधनविशेषः। उपमानस्यापि सखे प्रत्युपमानं वपुस्तस्याः॥** Vikram. II. 3; *cf*. also **इयमवयवैः पाण्डुक्षामैरलङ्कृतमण्डना** Mâl-Mádh. VI. 6.

 **P. 115.** **अनेन**— *sc*. **गरुडेन. एतत्**—*sc*. **शरीरम्. पूर्वम्**—*adv*. 'formerly', before it was mangled by Garuḍa. **परमार्थतः**— “in truth, if the fact were considered.'

 ** मेदोऽस्थि॰** etc.— Comparo with this s'l, the previous one **सर्वाशुचिनिधानस्य** etc. IV. 7. Construs **अस्मिन् सदाबीभत्सदर्शने** (of a disgusting sight) **त्वगावृते शरीरनाम्नि मेदोऽस्थि...सङ्घाते का शोभा. बीभत्स** (*adj*.) is derived from the desidor. of **बध्** I. Â. to loathe.

 ** नरकज्वाला॰**— At the thought of having committed a heinous crime the same prospect of hell rises before the mind of Garuḍa as did before that of S ́aṅkha. **(युक्त नेतुं भवतः पातालतलादपि तलं माम्** V. 19). He considerd himself as already in the grip of (**अवलीढ** *lit*, touched by) hell-fires. **दुःखं**—*adv*.; *cf*. **दुःखमास्ते विश्वावसुः** *supra* p. 94.

 **प्रतिपक्ष**—the usual sense of this word is 'an opponent, or adversary'; *cf. supra* **मतङ्गहतकस्ते प्रतिपक्षः** P. 8, **अयि प्रतिपक्षपातिनि** p. 59; here, however, it is used in a secondary sense, as equivalent to 'remedy,' 'atonement' (*i. e.,* something that will act like an enemy towards the sin by annihilating it).

 **नित्यं**—goes with **अभिघात** in the comp., ‘from thus daily killing the Nágas'. **प्रतिविरम**—desist; governs the abl. by **जुगुप्साविरामप्रमादार्थानाम् उपसङ्ख्यानम्** Vártika. **पुण्यप्रवाहं**—*lit*. a stream of holiness', hence a continuously growing store of merit. **अभीतिं**—safety (*lit*. freedom from fear); **दिशान्** granting. These two lines contain three of the principles of Buddhistic creed, *viz*., (1) **अहिंसा** (2) **अनुताप** and (3) **पुण्यसञ्चयन** by granting protection from fear.

 **P. 116. येन**—If you follow the course of conduct thus marked out. **अत्र मग्न एनः—अत्र** *sc*. **पुण्यप्रवाहे.** The student should observe the words **प्रवाह** and **मग्न** which have been intentionally used to accord with the simile in the last line. **परिणतं (सत्) न फलति**—will not bear fruit by being ripened, *i. e*., will not ripen so as to be ready to give fruit. According to the theory of Karman those actions only give fruit, which are ready for it; others being consigned to the domain of **सञ्चित.** Messrs. B. and P. say **‘पापत्वाभावेन परिणतं सत्** ‘losing its characteristics of a sin'; but it does not mean that; nor does the simile support this meaning. For the salt thrown into the water is not destroyed; it is made imperceptible: so the sin is made ineffective, *i, e.*, is not allowed to bring on its punishment. **परिणाम** according to the Vedânta philosophy means a change in which the proper form **(स्वरूप)** of the Prakṛiti is destroyed, as of milk when changed to cards; while **विवर्त** is a change in which the **प्रकृतिस्वरूप** remains unchanged, as in the case of water and bubbles. The rending **लवणकणामेव** athough it makes the simile more forcible is grammatically wrong as the word **कण** is *mas.*; and even though it be changed to **०कण इव** it will not do, as we require a word in the neu. gen. here to keep symmetry with **अंहः** which is nou, **दुर्गाधे** etc.—You should accumulate so much merit that your sin, being comparatively small in mass, will become submerged in it and become ineffective, just as a handful of salt thrown into a big reservoir of water is quite lost therein and is unable to make it salt in taste. **दुर्गाध**—unfathomable, same as **अगाध** **(गाध** means 'shallow' water, where it can be forded). **लवणपलं**—*lit*. ‘salt measuring a *pala* in weight, a handful of salt.’ A *pala* is a measure weighing about 1½ oz.

 **अद्य प्रभृति**—from to-day; *cf*. **अद्य प्रभृत्यवनताङ्गि तवास्मि दासः** Kum. V. 86. **अद्य प्रभृति**—**अस्मात् दिनात् आरभ्येत्यर्थः। प्रभृतियोगात् अद्येति सप्तम्यर्थवाचिना पञ्चम्यर्थो लक्ष्यते**। Malli. ad loc,

 **क्वचिदद्वीपा॰**—In this s'l. he describes the Nágas as they would appear to a looker-on when, being safe from Garuḍa, they would sport at pleasure in the ocean, **क्वचित्**— **क्वचित्** 'in this place— in that place'; *cf*. **क्वचित्पथा सञ्चरते सुराणां क्वचिद् घनानां पततां कचिश्च**। Ragh.
